Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department to Protect Overseas Chinese 32

(Tokyo) The Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department is giving special and careful consideration to the protection of Chinese residing in Japan. After consultation, it was decided that with respect to some who are connected to central departments in their home country, the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department will carry out strict crackdowns. On the other hand, those who are formally engaged in business will be resolutely protected. On the 26th, this directive was communicated to all the subordinate police stations. Currently, there are about 16,000 overseas Chinese in Japan, the majority of whom are students, followed by chefs, tailors, and barbers. Laborers constitute only a small minority. (26th, Allied News Agency)

French Foreign Minister's Speech to the League of Nations Advocates Restoring the Disarmament Conference, Hoping to End the Arms Race and Promote Political and Economic Progress 33

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly continued its meeting at 10:45 this morning. The chairman, Argentine representative Lamas, and French Foreign Minister Delbos delivered speeches advocating for arms reduction and proposing a meeting of the Disarmament Conference Bureau. He stated that world peace could be maintained through the League of Nations, and France firmly believes in this. France also agrees with the views expressed by British Foreign Secretary Eden yesterday: "Equality means listening to the views of small and weak nations. Fraternity means that when compromise and arbitration are still viable, force should not be used to resolve disputes. The current trend of dividing European countries into two opposing blocs based on ideological conflicts should be rejected." Delbos then spoke about the situation in Spain, stating that while France is not indifferent to the Spanish situation, it still advocates a policy of non-intervention. France fears that the competition among countries to supply arms to both sides in the Spanish civil war will inevitably lead to disputes. At this point, Delbos again advocated strengthening the League of Nations to prevent war. Regarding the implementation of Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant, France previously proposed that it could be implemented without unanimous approval by the Council, and the conclusion of regional mutual assistance pacts has already received the support of many countries, which is satisfactory. Regarding economic issues, their tense state should be eased as political stability improves. This is why France concluded currency agreements with the United Kingdom and the United States. It is hoped that an end to the arms race will mutually benefit political and economic improvement. Delbos then proposed that the meeting process could be summarized in three words: control, restriction, and reduction. In addition, each country should publish statistics on its own military status to demonstrate its sincerity for peace. If so, the acceptable level of armaments for each country can be determined, and proportional, parallel, and gradual arms reduction can be realized. As it stands now, some countries are already behind in the arms race and are doing their best to catch up, without knowing where it will end. It is hoped that all countries in the world can jointly consider ways to protect civilization. After Delbos finished speaking, the Norwegian representative and Foreign Minister Guthe took the floor, calling on the Assembly to concentrate its efforts on international cooperation. The Assembly adjourned at 12:30 pm. The Executive Council is scheduled to continue its meeting at 5:30 pm. (26th, Havas News Agency)

Rice Merchant Robbed on Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, Thief Escapes Through Train Window, Over Four Thousand Yuan Stolen 34

(Hangzhou) Zhang Zijie, a rice merchant from Jiangxi, was carrying over 4,200 yuan in cash today, traveling from Linpu to Jiangxi on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway. At 3:30 pm, while passing Jiangshan, he was suddenly robbed by a fellow passenger, who jumped out of the train window and escaped. There was no trace of the robber. The merchant has requested the local authorities to arrest the robber. (26th, Special Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegram, Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters on September 26th 35

Exchange Rates: The London foreign exchange market naturally felt unsettled after the devaluation of the French franc. This morning, everyone hesitated, and there was no trading. Exchange rates fluctuated wildly. The exchange rate against the Dutch guilder shrank to 7.30-7.35 today (yesterday it was 7.47-7.50). From this, it can be inferred that the exchange rate against the US dollar should be between $4.915 and $4.95.

This morning, official sources claimed that there would be no trading in the exchange market today, and gold prices would not be quoted.

It is rumored that Switzerland and Belgium will also participate in the monetary agreement between the United Kingdom, France, and the United States. This move reveals that Switzerland will also depreciate its franc.

Some now believe that the United Kingdom's goal is to bring the US dollar to $4.87. Leading figures in France are currently continuing to meet to decide what kind of national strength to adopt to cope with this new financial difficulty. The stock exchange is closed today.

Gold and Silver: London Large Bars: Today's spot and futures prices both rose by 25, to 19 shillings and 75 pence. American purchases, Indian and speculator trading are both in operation, and the market is stable.

Mountri Tailors: Because London rose by 25, the opening price for December futures rose by 5 pounds, to 44.55-44.97.

Securities: New York: The securities market opened with bullish sentiment due to news of the French franc devaluation. Most prices rose. The previous devaluation of the franc caused prices to fall, but the reason why it was able to raise prices this time is that a currency agreement was formed between the UK, the US and France. Belgium and Switzerland also followed this move, and other countries such as the Netherlands and Germany may join in the future. From this, it can be believed that world trade will definitely benefit from unity, and prices will also rise. The franc's devaluation and the pound's devaluation will have a slight impact on US exports. This matter has not yet been fully considered. The New York stock market prices are listed on the left:
